We enjoyed an intimate wedding ceremony provided by The Century. The Alcove was elegant, romantic, and whimsical. Our family enjoyed the atmosphere as well as the customer service provided. Allison was amazing on our wedding day and ensured things went smoothly. The food was delicious and served hot. My husband and I couldn't believe how The Century hosted a wonderful celebration for us to cherish forever. Allison took a ton of stress off our plates and we were able to enjoy the festivities. Although we had preferred a male officiant in the beginning, Crystal was phenomenal while implementing the wedding traditions we requested. She did a spectacular job of uniting our marriage. Our DJ was personable and fun! The music kept us entertained as we celebrated while enjoying each other's company. We are totally satisfied with the outcome and will never forget our magical day made possible by The Century!<//text>

< Text>
Given the pandemic, we decided on the new and popular micro-wedding as we did not want to further delay our wedding. As if things weren't challenging enough, we chose to get married in the month of February, when it's cold and usually rains. We had to find a venue that was Covid compliant and somehow still kept us protected from the outdoor elements and this was it. The Century wedding venue came up with a micro-wedding package at their location next door called Nine3One. Communication was great, all of our multiple inquiries, concerns and doubts were always responded to in a timely manner. Allison was our main contact person and she was always very pleasant to speak to even when we felt a little lost and anxious. It was hard for me to put into words what I wanted the setup to look like as far as the decorations, but let me tell you, they far exceeded our expectations. Everything was absolutely beautiful. My family said it was the best wedding food they had ever had, and our cake was so good we will return on our anniversary to order another. Allison took control of the flow of things during the whole event and it was nothing less than perfect. If we had the opportunity to do this again with any venue we would definitely still choose The Century. I don't know many people who can honestly say that their wedding day was perfect and went as planned, but I can! Thank you to all of the staff at The Century for making this happen for us. We will recommend you every chance we get.< /Text>

<user>110645736788481758819<//user>< Text>
I film weddings and events for a living and this was a really nice "all-in-one" venue. Really romantic lighting and decor. Plenty of space for family to lounge on. I felt the flowers needed to be in place much sooner, tho, because I needed to film it before guests came in. They were decorating up to the last moment. I'm not sure why the DJ's speakers were placed so close together on one side of the room. Speakers ought to be placed far apart for a more balanced sound (and less deafening for the table of guests seated nearest). The officiant flubbed his lines but I can clean up the video, I think. Overall, a very pleasant venue and parking is a breeze on a Sunday.</Text>

Did the elopement package here, beautiful venue with a rustic vibe. However, the photographer provided is not too good our photos came out low quality especially inside the venue and we didn't receive the photos until over a month later. The officiant messed up on our back story as we told them not to provide one and they gave us somebody else's random story. They also messed up on our guest list they didn't have the full list. Food, drinks, and cake was good. A/C is a little loud so people couldn't hear my vows and I am a soft spoken person as it is. The coordinator was very helpful the day of to let you know where to be.</Text>

Awesome community supermarket catering to the Jewish community, glatt.

The guy who runs the Deli in the back, Shimon is a miserable person and takes his unhappiness out on the employees and the customers. It's unfortunate.

The deli serves fresh made hummus to kabobs and all sorts of fresh food. My favorite is Harisa, a very spicy chili paste. Get a bit of it with whatever else you buy..

Very clean market. The prices are about 30% to 40% higher than other markets. < pics>
None<//pics>
<response>{'time': 1566754122782, 'text': "First of all, thank you for being a loyal ten year customer. It was nice speaking to you on Friday and I am sorry we don't see things eye to eye. I had thought that after our conversation we had come to an understanding.\n\nThe reason why some of the items cost 30-40% higher is because they are kosher items that have been imported from parts of the country or even from outside of the country. The shipping on these items are very expensive.\n\nIn addition, the items that are certified kosher go through special inspections to meet kosher standards. For example, broccoli, spinach and cauliflower go through a thorough inspection to make sure they are free of bugs. The same applies to cheeses which have certifications of their own. This leads to a significant increase in cost.\n\nIn regards to the moldy cheeses, the products we received come from smaller companies who use packaging methods that are not perfect. Sometimes air goes into the packaging. This leads to mold spots forming on the cheese.\n\nThe breads are handled by their respective bakeries. Usually someone from the bakery is supposed to remove all the old products and replace them with fresh products. Sometimes if a product from one bakery is left in a different section the bakery will miss a product. This is a rare occurrence and does not usually happen.\n\nWe try to remove all these products off the shelf to prevent customers from receiving them. In the event that a customer leaves with such products we will gladly offer them a refund.\n\nThank you for you time,\n\nAvraham Shamoil"}</response>< Gmap_id>

<review>All in all, a pretty decent food and beverage experience! Monte 52 is located inside of the Tropicana Market right in Highland Park. In fact, it almost seems to be multiple businesses in one...you have Monte 52 which takes care of your eating needs, a Kombucha/coffee/smoothie bar to the side which seems to be it's own entity, all located within this cute little market that sells everything from fresh produce to traditional and unique grocery items. It seems to be a very interesting business model, as you pay for all your separate food and drink items at the main counter for the market. This brought on an hour long convo between hubby and I about gentrification and how businesses can stay authentic yet stick with the times and stay relevant...but i digress haha.

Service was generally friendly but pretty slow. We did have to wait a bit for our food (but again, we were occupied and immersed in existential conversation), and we also had to flag down the kombucha lady as she was sitting in the back on her phone...by the time they found her, there were a few people waiting to place an order with her.

Food was decent - a few select breakfast dishes and vegan options available. We opted for a breakfast burrito, a Monte Cristo sandwich and a hash mash with soyrizo. I did enjoy the burrito but my hubby's sandwich was pretty soggy. The hash mash was also not bad but, in wrapping the food to bring to us, the wrapping warped so badly to the cheese that we lost all of it when it was time to eat and unwrap. Sad day. We did realllyyy enjoy the kombucha on tap though and highly recommend trying it! You can also purchase and fill growlers there as well!

I think i would be down to go back again and maybe try the place out for lunch!<//review><Name>Josefina Klein<//Name></record></dataset><record>

< Review>
Terrible customer service! I had placed my order via telephone prior to arrival. I waited in the store at the sandwich counter for at least 20minutes while consistently attempting to get an employees attention. Yes every one behind the counter seemed occupied and in motion, but common courtesy tells you to at least have one person taking orders or checking in with the customers waiting in line at the very least. Once I finally got the girls attention at the counter she litteraly just ignored me then proceeded to welcome a guy who just barged his way to the counter and said he was here for a postmates order (I guess thats what needs to be done to receive a response here). When the girl at the counter finally acknowledged me I was told my order was just waiting on the frys, so I waited, and waited... Throughout this wait I had decided to give the juice bar a try. I asked the guy working the juice bar counter what he'd recommend, his exact response was "Most of the drinks on the menu aren't even real, like for example we have an iced cappuccino but cappuccino is a foamy drink thats made from hot coffee therefore there is no such thing as an iced cappuccino." So I decided to try something new and ordered the Blended-Hortchata drink. The employees response was "oh we actually dont have Hortchata and ironically never have" in a very serious tone I proceed to inquire as to why it's even listed as an option on menu then? I mean clearly it says Blended- Caramel, Mocha, Hortchata.. His response was nothing more than a mere chuckle and scratch on his head. So finally I gave up and ordered just a plain mocha blend (Frappuccino) nothing special right? But it doesn't stop there, instead the same employee litteraly tells me "oh I dont know how to make that kind of drink, so my coworkers going to help you out ok" then he proceededs to make his own ice coffee in front of me, walk away and sit down in the corner, didnt even mention my order, I had to tell the poor other hard working lady (whom I am sure carries out 90% of the shifts duties all on her own) what my order was. Not to mention the guy who originally was helping me (suppose to be of help) didn't even take this as an opportunity to learn how to blend a Frappuccino, he simply just turned the whole responsibility over to his coworker and decided to take a break. Anyhow..
At this point I was super fed up already, finally grabbed my sandwich order (which was already 22minutes OVER what they estimated to me on the phone) and left. Arrived home ate extremely cold and soggy food (tasted like it had been sitting for hours) and to no avail... NO french frys in the bag! (That's what I'd been waiting for!)
I swear these employees must have been high, drunk, or out right careless; It's the only plausible explanation! This is a shame because I had high expectations coming in after all the buzz going around town and hearing good things coming from close friends and family members. I don't like to come off as if I'm attacking any one particular business when I do these reviews, but when I have an experience such as this one, I believe my experience needs to be put into perspective.< /Review>

< rate>

<text>All in all, a pretty decent food and beverage experience! Monte 52 is located inside of the Tropicana Market right in Highland Park. In fact, it almost seems to be multiple businesses in one...you have Monte 52 which takes care of your eating needs, a Kombucha/coffee/smoothie bar to the side which seems to be it's own entity, all located within this cute little market that sells everything from fresh produce to traditional and unique grocery items. It seems to be a very interesting business model, as you pay for all your separate food and drink items at the main counter for the market. This brought on an hour long convo between hubby and I about gentrification and how businesses can stay authentic yet stick with the times and stay relevant...but i digress haha.

Service was generally friendly but pretty slow. We did have to wait a bit for our food (but again, we were occupied and immersed in existential conversation), and we also had to flag down the kombucha lady as she was sitting in the back on her phone...by the time they found her, there were a few people waiting to place an order with her.

Food was decent - a few select breakfast dishes and vegan options available. We opted for a breakfast burrito, a Monte Cristo sandwich and a hash mash with soyrizo. I did enjoy the burrito but my hubby's sandwich was pretty soggy. The hash mash was also not bad but, in wrapping the food to bring to us, the wrapping warped so badly to the cheese that we lost all of it when it was time to eat and unwrap. Sad day. We did realllyyy enjoy the kombucha on tap though and highly recommend trying it! You can also purchase and fill growlers there as well!

I think i would be down to go back again and maybe try the place out for lunch!<//text>< Pictures>

<Pics>None</Pics>< Name>
Willful Serenity< /Name>
<Review>The definition of insanity is doing the same thing over and over, yet expecting different results...and right now, I feel I must be going crazy, because I keep coming to this convenient location and expecting the experience to be positive.¬† I have honestly lost count of the number of times my drink has either tasted bad, or the order was wrong, or a number of other small irritating things have occurred.¬† The only consistency that I have experienced here is that the baristas have shown a consistent lack of care towards their customers.¬† Each time I go to this location, I question myself - is the covenience of the drive thru worth the poorly executed drink and careless attitude if the baristas?

To be fair, there are maybe two great baristas there - but the majority of them seem to be pretty unhappy, and as a result, the service ends up sucking.  I don't know why.  Perhaps it's a management issue?  Either way, it seems to be a perfect example of "water seeks its own level".  They are uniformly unpleasant or incompetent.  It's like, if Starbucks had a hell, this location would be Purgatory.

Here are only a few examples:

I have overheard one of their regular baristas - an extremely thin young man with pale complexion and spiky hair - actually encourage the barista at the drive thru window to lie to a customer who was behind me ("Just tell her it's decaf, she won't notice."  I happen to have a friend who is extremely sensitive to caffeine, and its disturbs me to know that the workers here have no qualms about potentially hurting someone).¬† I have had that same barista lie to my face and insist - after I returned an incorrect order to them and repeated my original request - that there was no difference to the cost between the two items (when their menu shows there's a 35 cent difference).  They have added things to my beverages (sweetener when I have requested none) or given me completely different drinks than what I ordered ("iced grande mocha" is very different from "matcha green tea Frappuccino").¬† Baristas rarely give receipts and are immediately dismissive of the customer after they've handed out the drink order.¬† Often the drink tastes weak, bitter, or just plain old (similar to sucking on coffee grounds).

It's been two years of sucking...and I know I keep saying this to myself, but convenience be damned: this is, by far, consistently the worst Starbucks I have ever gone to...and I will not return.  Just bought yet another fetid, oddly viscous coffee from there, and I'm NOT GOING BACK. I had to throw out the last two, and this one is heading for the trash as well.

If you want to know of a location that is amazing and makes drinking Starbucks a treat, consider Safeway on Bell Rd in Auburn.¬† Despite being a grocery store location, their coffee (and the service) is consistently excellent.  I also think the drive thru on Foresthill exit is awesome, asbis the Target Bell Rd location.< /Review>< Response>
